Takayama is famous for its historic Sanmachi-Suji district, with many wooden shops dating back to the Edo period. Takayama is a popular destination in the winter, boasting natural hot spring sources with numerous ryokans (Japanese-style inns) offering onsen (hot spring) relaxation. Staying at a Ryokan and experiencing an onsen in the winter here is truly fascinating. From Takayama, it's just a 40-minute bus ride to the historic village of Shirakawago, making Takayama a great base for exploring UNESCO heritage, but Takayama itself is also a delightful destination for visitors to enjoy.\n\nHere are some of the best activities to do when visiting Takayama that you shouldn't miss:\n\nThe red bridge crossing the Miya-gawa river connects Sanmachi-Suji to the rest of the city and is reminiscent of Kyoto's Gion. In the Sanmachi-Suji district, Edo-era houses still stand, and the area is always bustling with locals and visitors. Even in the crowds, you can hear the sound of the nearby Miya-gawa river. In the spring, festivals are held along the river, creating a lively atmosphere. In the historic district, you can find renowned Hida beef sushi and local sweets, as well as souvenirs.\nSanmachi-Suji is only a 15-minute walk from JR Takayama Station, and in the evenings, you can find excellent yakiniku (grilled meat) and shabu shabu restaurants. However, the most famous are the Hida beef sushi shops, which often have long lines. Sanmachi-Suji is also home to traditional sake breweries inside wooden houses, adding to the area's unique charm.\n\nEnjoy Premium Hida Beef Hida beef is a premium Japanese beef brand that competes with Kobe and Matsuzaka beef for the title of the best beef in Japan. These three brands make up the top tier of Japanese beef. Kobe beef is the most internationally recognized, while Hida beef is less exported. Hida beef is designated for beef that meets quality grades A/B and ranks 5/4/3, and it is raised in Gifu Prefecture. The name \"Hida\" comes from the Hida region surrounding Takayama. When you arrive in Takayama, you can simply search on Google Maps for Hida beef restaurants, and you will find plenty of options.\n\nTo savor Hida beef, there are various preparation methods to choose from, with yakiniku (grilled meat) and sushi (slices of beef on rice) being the most popular. You can also opt for shabu-shabu, although some find it less enjoyable.\nAddress for Hida beef sushi: Hida Kotte Ushi, 34 Kamisannomachi, Takayama, Gifu 506-0846, Japan: The most famous and usually crowded, with a wait time of 20-30 minutes, the price is 650 JPY for 2 pieces of sushi.\n\nStay in a Ryokan and Enjoy Onsen Takayama has natural hot spring sources from the nearby mountains, making it a famous destination for onsen, especially in the winter. If you want to enjoy onsen, you can choose public bathhouses, but for a more authentic experience, stay at a Ryokan, a traditional Japanese inn. I chose Oyado Hachibei, which is a 15-minute taxi ride from JR Takayama Station. The inn features indoor onsens, but the most famous is the outdoor onsen, which is incredibly relaxing. When you visit, don't forget to wear a yukata to fully immerse yourself in traditional Japanese surroundings. Th\u1ea7n nu\u00f4i l\u00f2ng h\u1eadn th\u00f9 nhi\u1ec1u n\u0103m, hay tin vua l\u00ean n\u00fai th\u1ec9nh thi\u1ec1n s\u01b0 b\u00e8n t\u00ecm \u0111\u1ebfn ph\u1ee5c k\u00edch ngay c\u00e1nh r\u1eebng, \u0111\u1ee3i \u0111\u1ee9c vua \u0111i xu\u1ed1ng s\u1ebd h\u1ea1 s\u00e1t tr\u1ea3 th\u00f9 cho anh. Ch\u1eb3ng may trong l\u00fac mai ph\u1ee5c b\u1ecb tr\u01b0\u1ee3t ch\u00e2n t\u00e9 ng\u00e3 v\u00e0 tr\u1ecdng th\u01b0\u01a1ng, ch\u1ec9 c\u00f2n c\u00e1ch duy nh\u1ea5t l\u00e0 ch\u1ea1y l\u00ean \u0111\u1ec9nh n\u00fai c\u1ea7u c\u1ee9u. C\u0169ng may ph\u01b0\u1edbc l\u1edbn m\u1ea1ng l\u1edbn \u0111\u01b0\u1ee3c vua v\u00e0 thi\u1ec1n s\u01b0 t\u1eadn t\u00ecnh c\u1ee9u ch\u1eefa, nay th\u1ea7n \u0111\u00e3 tho\u00e1t ch\u1ebft, c\u1ea7u xin b\u1ec7 h\u1ea1 h\u00e3y tha t\u1ed9i khi qu\u00e2n ph\u1ea1m th\u01b0\u1ee3ng.\n\u0110\u1ee9c vua bu\u1ed3n b\u00e3 bi\u1ebft r\u1eb1ng h\u00f3a ra m\u1ecdi s\u1ef1 \u0111\u1ec1u l\u00e0 do sai l\u1ea7m qu\u00e1 kh\u1ee9 c\u1ee7a b\u1ea3n th\u00e2n, vua tha t\u1ed9i cho ch\u00e0ng trai. C\u01a1 duy\u00ean g\u1eb7p g\u1ee1 n\u00e0y \u0111\u00e3 h\u00f3a gi\u1ea3i ho\u00e0n to\u00e0n m\u1ed1i th\u00e2m th\u00f9 c\u1ee7a ch\u00e0ng trai d\u00e0nh cho vua. Sau khi m\u1ecdi s\u1ef1 t\u1ecf b\u00e0y v\u1edbi ch\u00e0ng trai, vua b\u00e8n h\u1ecfi thi\u1ec1n s\u01b0 l\u1ea7n cu\u1ed1i:\n- Thi\u1ec1n s\u01b0 n\u1ebfu bi\u1ebft xin h\u00e3y tr\u1ea3 l\u1eddi cho ta BA C\u00c2U H\u1eceI \u0111\u00f3, b\u1eb1ng kh\u00f4ng ta l\u1eadp t\u1ee9c xu\u1ed1ng n\u00fai.\n- Ta \u0111\u00e3 tr\u1ea3 l\u1eddi cho b\u1ec7 h\u1ea1 r\u1ed3i \u0111\u1ea5y th\u00f4i.\n- Tr\u1eabm th\u1eadt t\u00ecnh kh\u00f4ng hi\u1ec3u.\n- TH\u1edcI GIAN N\u00c0O L\u00c0 QUAN TR\u1eccNG NH\u1ea4T? Chi\u1ec1u qua \u0111\u1ee9c vua mu\u1ed1n g\u1eb7p ta th\u00ec ta l\u00e0 quan tr\u1ecdng nh\u1ea5t c\u00f2n t\u1ed1i h\u00f4m qua, hai ch\u00fang ta c\u00f9ng c\u1ee9u ng\u01b0\u1eddi b\u1ecb th\u01b0\u01a1ng n\u00e0y th\u00ec ch\u00e0ng trai n\u00e0y l\u00e0 quan tr\u1ecdng nh\u1ea5t.\n- C\u00d4NG VI\u1ec6C N\u00c0O L\u00c0 QUAN TR\u1eccNG NH\u1ea4T?
